<div id="review_2755371375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2755371375" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2755371375?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2019">z-faves2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2019">y-out2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2019">z-read2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2755371375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8201037288059084864">I really just binge reread this book in an hour and a half. I don’t know why any of you talk to me<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>As usual, the day guard at the Dirksen Building glares at him as he slides through security. She’s certain he was the one who vandalized the sign outside one particular senator’s office to read BITCH MCCONNELL, but she’ll never prove it.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>A ridiculous romance between the made-up prince of England and the made-up son of the made-up first woman president has no right to be this <i>good</i>. And yet</span>
  <span id="freeText8201037288059084864" style="display:none">I really just binge reread this book in an hour and a half. I don’t know why any of you talk to me<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>As usual, the day guard at the Dirksen Building glares at him as he slides through security. She’s certain he was the one who vandalized the sign outside one particular senator’s office to read BITCH MCCONNELL, but she’ll never prove it.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />A ridiculous romance between the made-up prince of England and the made-up son of the made-up first woman president has no right to be this <i>good</i>. And yet.<br /><br />For those of you wondering if I’m joking about the premise of this book, I am completely not. It’s escapism to a world where American politics are at their normal level of messed up, but. You know. The election went in a different direction. (The popular vote direction, just like, by the way.) <br /><br />It’s a book about the importance of loving in a world very very desperate to tear down love. The use of historical love letters… OOF. Radclyffe Hall to Evguenia Souline, Alexander Hamilton to John Laurens, Eleanor Roosevelt to Lorena Hickock, Michelangelo to Tommaso Cavalieri, Wilfred Owen to Siegfried Sassoon, Jean Cocteaua to Jean Marais. I will say it: the Vita-Sackville-West-to-Virginia-Woolf letter is absolutely one of my favorite pieces of writing of all time and makes me cry daily. And the line “history, huh?” got me. <br /><br />And it’s a book about love as a choice. The line “On purpose. I love him on purpose.” has reached an almost memetic level on Tumblr and Twitter, but I <i>get it.</i> There are so many narratives, especially in queer lit, about love as something choiceless. But the thing is love is always a choice. And when you find the right person, it’s a good one. <br /><br />It helps that the cast of characters is just really excellent. Alex and Henry are both really well-written characters, but Alex’s narration is genuinely incredibly hilarious. I laugh easily, but I’ve found that writing good humor can be kind of hard, and this worked for me. Nora and June are each good side characters. I also really appreciated characters like Bea, Pez, and Zahra, who show up briefly but make an impact anyway. <br /><br />But. that is why this is objectively ridiculous romance novel resonated with me harder than 90% of the books I’ve read this year, as a lesbian who is almost definitely going to major in history or polisci (or both, I have another year). It’s about the tenderness and also about the weight of expressing love and also about how both our global context and our community history unite and bind us as queer people. <br /><br />I’m done. Time to scream, with spoilers. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>some lines and moments from this book I will be thinking about a lot:</i>
</b><br /><br />➽“So, if he and Nora occasionally get drunk in hotel rooms together watching The West Wing and making loud moaning noises at the wall for the benefit of nosy tabloids, he can’t be blamed, really. They’re simply turning an undesirable situation into their own personal entertainment.”<br />➽I only started writing these down in the second half but Alex’s bi crisis… i get it. i really do<br />➽I don’t know<br />➽“It’s a week. The polls aren’t great, Paul Ryan is getting sanctimonious about the second amendment,”<br />➽the tenderness of the phone call scene<br />➽the bar scene like god that’s friendship babes!<br />➽“I’m going for like depressed lesbian poet who met a hot yoga instructor at a speakeasy who got her super into meditation and pottery and now she’s starting a new life as a high powered businesswoman selling her own line of hand-thrown fruit bowls”<br />➽“I thought you just got into international politics or something” “well, technically,”<br />➽“her son’s fucking quarter life NATO sexual crisis”<br />➽the PowerPoint presentation had me CRYING<br />➽“the phrase see attached bibliography is the single sexiest thing you have ever written to me” like I’m sorry what a fucking mood<br />➽“American politics: truly fascinating” “you wanna talk, Henry VIII?”<br />➽when Henry swan-dives into a lake and inwardly Alex is like he’s so gorgeous and outwardly Alex is like “do you have to be so goddamn extra”<br />➽actually that entire lake scene is just like... so romantic I’m out here wanting a wife<br />➽the forty seven texts ending up being 46 from June and one from Nora asking where she left her shoes<br />➽”consciously? subconsciously, in total detail?” is just such a relatable statement<br />➽the Prince consort road<br />➽“Take a picture with me with the sign!”<br />➽“The top list of reasons to love you goes brain, then dick, then imminent status as a revolutionary gay icon”<br />➽the sheer amount of times Alex threatens to physically fight someone<br />➽sometimes it’s for Henry’s honor but most of the time it’s not<br />➽“lmaooooooooooo wait look at page 22 of the emails alex is such a hoe”<br />➽everything Zahra does in this entire book<br />➽also everything Bea does in this entire book<br />➽Henry’s speech to Philip aka one of the single most legendary things I’ve ever read<br />➽“plus, we banged it out last night”<br />➽Henry’s mom really came in and saved their asses like that she did that and she did it for us (the gays)<br />➽history, huh?<br />➽that fucking TWEET about DC dykes on bikes chasing down the westboro baptist church<br />➽“Sufia, am I allowed to say that?” “literally, when has that ever stopped you?”<br />➽Amy and her wife!!!!!!!! at the parade!! <br />➽this doesn’t really have to do with the book but please Texas. please become a swing state faster. I know you’re on your way but it would be really kind and generous of you to go blue in 2020. please<br /><br /><a href="https://ellexamines.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/ellexamines/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4F6I" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://ellexamines.carrd.co/#about" rel="nofollow noopener">About</a> |</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2738849511?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=my-heart-is-on-the-carpet">my-heart-is-on-the-carpet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=panty-dropper">panty-dropper</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=never-forget">never-forget</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2738849511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5827991596109282821"><i>
  <b>“But the truth is, also, simply this: love is indomitable."</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551886757i/27163432.jpg' width='500' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551886757ra/27163433.gif' width='500' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b><br/>My heart is so entirely full, it's nearly overflowing. This book was in a word; matchless. I laughed, I loved, I cried but mostly loved every beautiful little thing that led up to the last page. Now, having finished, I wish for nothing more but to go all the way back to the beginning and start again. As readers, sometimes -<i>very rarely</i>- you come across a book that quintessentially becomes a mantra, a new sense of hope and a burst of s</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5827991596109282821" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“But the truth is, also, simply this: love is indomitable."</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551886757i/27163432.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551886757ra/27163433.gif" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><br>My heart is so entirely full, it's nearly overflowing. This book was in a word; matchless. I laughed, I loved, I cried but mostly loved every beautiful little thing that led up to the last page. Now, having finished, I wish for nothing more but to go all the way back to the beginning and start again. As readers, sometimes -<i>very rarely</i>- you come across a book that quintessentially becomes a mantra, a new sense of hope and a burst of something you never really knew existed. <br>I don't think I will ever forget this novel. <br></b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537629625i/26337778._SX540_.jpg" width="600" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>_______________<br><br><u>
  <b>On the off chance this book hasn't already won you over... </b>
</u><br><br>For a glimpse on my current situation: <br>i'm sporting sweatpants, haven't cooked for more than 24 hours, hair's an absolute mess, feel like screaming how gay i am out the window, and completely abandoned my responsibilities. <br><b>my horoscope did not prepare me for this. </b><br><br>When this book is published, and readers pick it up for the first time, I'm going to be sitting and watching all the emotions unfurl and all the fan;art,fiction,girling commence. And while I sit and watch, I'm going to be so jealous of everyone that has the luxury of reading this for the first time. <br><br>It's equal parts funny and loving and clever and tragic. I made a note on my kindle at page 3 stating "this is it," because that's how much I could feel the energy of a fucking brilliant book in my hands. The camaraderie and friendship combined with rebellion and sexy banter is almost too good to be in one novel. This is quite possibly the easiest five stars I have <b>
  <i>ever</i>
</b> given. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"So, you can hate the heir to the throne all you want, write mean poems about him in your diary, but the minute you see a camera, you act like the sun shines out of his dick, and you make it convincing.” <br>“Have you met Henry?” Alex says. “How am I supposed to do that? He has the personality of a cabbage.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551982916i/27169203._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>A Tribute</b>
</u><br><br>In more ways than one, the story behind Alex and Henry's relationship is magic. There is quite a lot of politics involved, quite a lot of drunkedness and quite a lot of soft moments that make you clutch your kindle slightly tighter. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"But he thinks about Henry, and, oh. He thinks about Henry, and something twists in his chest, like a stretch he’s been avoiding for too long."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>This was an enemies to lovers romance with so much more going for it. A beautiful feeling arose throughout the book as I saw the family and the omnipresent feeling of hope through friends. Nora gave me life and made me swoon. June was someone we all need in our life, alongside Pez. Bea was the softest cinnamon role in the whole bakery and when they were all together, my heart started singing. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Alexander, babes,” Pez says when he picks up. “How lovely for you to give your auntie Pezza a ring on this magnificent Sunday morning.” He’s smiling from what looks like the passenger seat of a luxury car, wearing a cartoonishly large sunhat and a striped pashmina."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I wish I could go up to every one that will ever have doubts about reading this book and beg them to give it a chance. Sometimes, I'm skeptical about picking up new authors - especially, when they are debuting with a genre that means so much to me. Yet, here I am, falling incredibly in love with everything this book is and will continue to be in my life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Never tell me the odds."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_3037218240" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3037218240" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3037218240?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook " href="/book/show/50019694-red-white-royal-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3037218240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15756098656384018733">4.5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/15/red-white-royal-blue-by-casey-mcquiston/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><b>BONUS:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/15/red-white-royal-blue-by-casey-mcquiston/' rel='nofollow noopener'>At the end, there are 10 quotes proving that Zahra is the ultimate mood</a> !!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591444214i/29602780._SY540_.jpg' width='248' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>I’d be so happy right now to actually have proper words to describe this beautiful mess that this book is but I rarely do have them so this review is going to be an equally hot mess. I’m actually having a doughnut while writing this so that should do.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Red, White & Royal Blue</b>
</i> is not exactly my type of reading. I mean, I had doubts I’d possibly like this kind </span>
  <span id="freeText15756098656384018733" style="display:none">4.5/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/15/red-white-royal-blue-by-casey-mcquiston/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><b>BONUS:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/15/red-white-royal-blue-by-casey-mcquiston/" rel="nofollow noopener">At the end, there are 10 quotes proving that Zahra is the ultimate mood</a> !!<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591444214i/29602780._SY540_.jpg" width="248" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I’d be so happy right now to actually have proper words to describe this beautiful mess that this book is but I rarely do have them so this review is going to be an equally hot mess. I’m actually having a doughnut while writing this so that should do.<br><br><i>
  <b>Red, White &amp; Royal Blue</b>
</i> is not exactly my type of reading. I mean, I had doubts I’d possibly like this kind of fiction, and the synopsis didn’t quite help me in that area. But you guys (yeah, you, the ones who read it and fell in obsession with it) made me want to give it a try with your exuberance.<br><br><b>AND I BLOODY LOVED IT.</b><br><br>Really, after the first chapter I was like <i>girl, keep reading, why the hell you stopped?</i><br><br>It made me feel excruciatingly giggly.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483711209ra/21641771.gif" width="348" height="239" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What made it super pleasant for me is the twist of the political reality – the United States actually has a female president, which is a determined lady from Texas and she has two amazing children who happen to be half Mexican. How cool is that though?<br><br>On the other hand, I found a bit of time and event inaccuracy in this that actually disturbs my OCD and keeps me awake at night.<br>At first, I thought the action was happening by the end of 2019 and then some mumbo-jumbo happens and we’re in the middle of 2020 somehow and no one <i>but absolutely no one</i> gives a shit about the fact that the 2020 Olympics are <i>happening</i> then.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503828704ra/23696566.gif" width="362" height="205" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, those are details that would probably be discussed by me with a shrink in a private session of why am I like this. Let me show you instead another positive thing about this book that I really loved.<br><br>These characters, man. These characters are EVERYTHING, I swear.<br><br>They all are so sweet and so witty and so lovely and they make you feel so warm and welcome. They’re just a bunch of nutters. It’s like you have everything you need in a handful of persons:<br><br>- Strong mums who love their children and help them and support them no matter what;<br>- Equally amazing father figures with whom I’d actually enjoy having a beer;<br>- Fabulously beautiful and intelligent and daring girls who are the world’s best sisters and can easily be your best friends (and I mean all of them, June, Bea, Nora);<br>- Two terribly sweet boys who are so pure and so dirty and so completely mad at the same time I’ll personally unleash hell for them if that’s what’ll make them feel safe;<br><br>(Also, teeny-tiny thingy here: I TOTALLY COULD FEEL HENRY IS A PIECES AND ALEX IS AN ARIES. I could feel it in my bones, I swear. Henry is as slightly introverted and as prone to extreme mood swings and as puppy-lovable like every Pieces I know and Alex is as stubborn and as passionate and ready to take over the world, making plans, being the centre of every event, burying himself in thousands of projects as every single Aries I know. Jesus, this is disturbingly accurate.)<br><br>- The ultimate eccentric best friend who is like that one person you’d love to spend time with and know he’s going to force you to have a good time and you’ll love it aka Pez;<br>- A gay Latino Skittles-eating guardian angel aka Rafael Luna (even his name is full of essence);<br>- Zahra – the biggest fucking mood in the entire Universe;<br><br>All of the characters are part of this amazing feeling you get while reading the book, it’s something cosy and familiar and warm.<br><br>The love in this book is real and is tear-dropping. But still, let me warn you about some aspects.<br><br>There are <b>loads</b> of hook-ups and sexy-scenes in there, some more detailed, some not-so, but you still get the picture. Dead-ass serious now, to me, they are a bit cringe. But not because of a boy loving another boy. God no. To me, scenes like that, with an <i>explicit</i> type of content, are cringe as hell in general. No matter in which -sexuality suffix they end.<br><br>So. This was a lit book. I loved it. Even more than I thought. And while reading it, I didn’t care who fell in love with whom and everything. I actually forgot about all these stereotypes and labels the society tries to push down our throats. For moments on, there was just me, witnessing a love story unfolding. And this was fucking amazing because, being from a socially and mentally constipated country, I don’t get to see acts of freedom like that. Which <b>scream</b> at me with love.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I thought, this is the most incredible thing I have ever seen, and I had better keep it a safe distance away from me. I thought, if someone like you ever loved me, it would set me on fire. And then I was a careless fool, and I fell in love with you anyway (…). And then, inexplicably, you had the absolute audacity to love me back. Can you believe it?”</b>
</i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581954283i/28977701.png" width="320" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/928a4c1b-a86c-4227-ba69-a1bd4c128c00_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15756098656384018733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2659405374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11493222667795111698"><b>
  <i>History, huh?</i>
</b><br/><br/>To be honest, I wasn't expecting to love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41150487.Red__White___Royal_Blue' title='Red, White & Royal Blue by Casey McQuiston' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red, White & Royal Blue</a>. I mean, this is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17949486.Casey_McQuiston' title='Casey McQuiston' rel='nofollow noopener'>Casey McQuiston</a>'s first book, and it's written in <i>present tense</i> (ugh), but love it I did. I loved it HARD. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41150487.Red__White___Royal_Blue' title='Red, White & Royal Blue by Casey McQuiston' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red, White & Royal Blue</a> was everything I was looking for and more.<br/><br/><b>My reading experience was simply me laughing, crying, or swooning in a continuous cycle. Sometimes all three at once.</b> It's been a long, long time since I've wanted to melt into a puddle of goo on the floor because the <i>romance!!!</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11493222667795111698" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>History, huh?</i>
</b><br /><br />To be honest, I wasn't expecting to love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41150487.Red__White___Royal_Blue" title="Red, White &amp; Royal Blue by Casey McQuiston" rel="nofollow noopener">Red, White &amp; Royal Blue</a>. I mean, this is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17949486.Casey_McQuiston" title="Casey McQuiston" rel="nofollow noopener">Casey McQuiston</a>'s first book, and it's written in <i>present tense</i> (ugh), but love it I did. I loved it HARD. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41150487.Red__White___Royal_Blue" title="Red, White &amp; Royal Blue by Casey McQuiston" rel="nofollow noopener">Red, White &amp; Royal Blue</a> was everything I was looking for and more.<br /><br /><b>My reading experience was simply me laughing, crying, or swooning in a continuous cycle. Sometimes all three at once.</b> It's been a long, long time since I've wanted to melt into a puddle of goo on the floor because the <i>romance!!!</i><b> Holy god, this story was the romancey-romance of your dreams.</b><br /><br />I'm a sucker for a few things in a romance book, and this story has nearly <i>all</i> of them. We get a <b>sexual awakening</b> (can I get a <i>halleloo</i>?!), an <b>enemies-to-lovers</b> (with all the glorious <i>damn, your face</i>, bruising kissing that I could dream up), <b>witty banter for <i>daaaaaaaaaaays</i></b>, and a romance with a literal (okay, fictional... but still) <b>PRINCE OF MOTHER FORKING ENGLAND</b>. Did <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17949486.Casey_McQuiston" title="Casey McQuiston" rel="nofollow noopener">Casey McQuiston</a> worm her way into my brain and pull out my deepest fantasies?!?!?!<br /><br />I wanted to take a nap inside these pages. I took pictures and screenshots of my Kindle of the uber-romantic email exchange to swoon over later. I cried and laughed like a lunatic on my couch, huddled in a prison of tea and reading of my own making. I fell asleep with the imprint of my Kindle on my face at 3 am. <br /><br /><b>Even though I don't like reading about politics or political games, even though present tense makes me feel itchy (did I mention that yet??), and even though the sex scenes are suggestive but still fade-to black I wanted to read this book FOREVER.</b><br /><br />The dialogue is something I will remember for a long time. The <i>humor</i> was absolutely everything and elevated this book from good to unbelievably amazing. The feelings were so intense I felt like my heart was going to jump out of my chest. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41150487.Red__White___Royal_Blue" title="Red, White &amp; Royal Blue by Casey McQuiston" rel="nofollow noopener">Red, White &amp; Royal Blue</a> is worth all the hype and more. It's worth your time and your money, and it's worth it to read something so <b>fun and heartfelt and rare</b> that it made it's way on to my elusive favorites list. With literally thousands of romances under my belt, this one still stands out. <br /><br /><i>And nothing will matter but just we two, we two longing loves at last come together.</i><br /><br />*Copy provided in exchange for an honest review*<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time" rel="nofollow noopener">goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.instagram.com/reading_all_night_long/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a>|<a href="https://twitter.com/DentistHeatherK" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>|<a href="http://www.myfictionnook.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2710108952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2710108952" />
    <a title="Madison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19576767-madison"><img alt="Madison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484592765p2/19576767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2710108952?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madison" href="/user/show/19576767-madison">Madison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2710108952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5444542250419328109">I recieved this book from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>This book is going to avoid rightful criticism because it’s a “fun, fluffy” romance novel and “isn’t supposed to be that serious.” There’s no denying that a lighthearted story about two men falling in love is sorely missing on mainstream shelves, but we need to ask ourselves why this is the book that got picked for the “Nicholas Sparks treatment”--the $16.99 retail price, the mainstream publisher, all of the things most modern </span>
  <span id="freeText5444542250419328109" style="display:none">I recieved this book from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />This book is going to avoid rightful criticism because it’s a “fun, fluffy” romance novel and “isn’t supposed to be that serious.” There’s no denying that a lighthearted story about two men falling in love is sorely missing on mainstream shelves, but we need to ask ourselves why this is the book that got picked for the “Nicholas Sparks treatment”--the $16.99 retail price, the mainstream publisher, all of the things most modern romance novels don’t get, particularly ones with LGBTQ characters. I mean, seriously, can you think of one contemporary author outside of YA who has gotten famous writing LGBTQ romance novels? What about fiction in general? I know, me neither. It’s depressing as hell. So why this book? It’s not because it’s actually good. That much is for damn sure.<br /> I have a theory. We’ll get to that in a bit. <br />Red, White, and Royal Blue follows Alex Claremont-Diaz, a Mexican-American kid whose mom was elected president in 2016. We’re supposed to conceive of this book as a sort of gay Chasing Liberty meets Parks and Recreation: a heartfelt, optimistic, unfailingly patriotic romp where the stars are, yeah, two hot dudes, but they’re carried on the broad, benevolent shoulders of Lady Liberty. <br />President Ellen Claremont is a white, Southern, centrist Democrat--because, sure, this is an alternate universe, but let’s not go wild--with two children, wannabe journalist June and politics-obsessed Alex. Alex’s arch nemesis for about 5 percent of the book is Prince Henry of Wales, and then he’s his secret boyfriend for the next 90 percent. At the end, they’re outed by Ellen’s political rival, which results in him soundly losing the election against her and turning Texas blue.<br />CM writes in the acknowledgements that this book started as a fun project and, after the course of the actual 2016 election, became a sort of therapeutic, wish-fulfilling exercise. I get that; I wrote fanfiction about Pete Wentz being my boyfriend in the 6th grade, so why not a President!Hillary AU? I don’t begrudge her that. My issue is that someone else picked up this book and thought it was a good idea to publish it.<br />There are so many little things that make this book bad: the fact that Alex and Henry are “arch rivals” for literally about ten pages until they’re kissing, and then there’s no plot for a hundred pages; this whole minor plotline where the First Family gets caught with a private email server that reads like a smug joke (“maybe this would matter in some OTHER America, but not this one!”); Alex wearing a red white and blue Gucci bomber jacket instead of a suit as if it’s some world-ending transgression; when the First Family and two of the royal siblings go to a gay bar in West Hollywood and no other patrons post any photos or sell any quotes to gossip magazines...I could honestly go on forever. These are the stupid things we’re not supposed to criticize because this is a “fun” book, so I won’t.<br />How about instead, we talk about when Henry says “I’d rather be waterboarded...Your country could probably arrange that,” and we’re supposed to see that as a cute zinger. Or when Ellen says “My UN ambassador...said something idiotic about Israel, so now I have to call Netanyahu and personally apologize.” And then we move on to pizza and beer. The problem with this book isn’t just that it’s overly precious and poorly paced; the problem is that it is trying to be both Veep and House of Cards. It exists in a world where we are to believe that a prince “refusing the crown’s money” (as if he isn’t steeped in it, as if he doesn’t benefit from it every minute he’s alive) is somehow the apex of morality. It exists in an America where email servers don’t matter in an election. It exists in a Britain where a prince would say “One does not foster a lifelong love of Star Wars without knowing an ‘empire’ isn’t a good thing.” These cutesy one-liners and feel-good plotlines do nothing to contend with the imperial violence they’re hinting at, violence from which Alex and Henry both benefit. Okay, so Ellen chats with Netanyahu and June wants to be bffs with Ronan Farrow. Following these fun details to their logical conclusion, I can only assume that Ellen orders drone strikes in the Middle East and Henry’s grandmother is a violent racist. If I were supposed to be having a good time reading, that notion would certainly jerk me out of it quickly. The point this book misses is that it doesn’t matter how liberal the President is—the system is still a gruesome, ever-grinding machine. This book isn’t absolved from that reality, not when it makes glib references to war criminals and WikiLeaks.<br />If this book had leaned harder into its Disney Channel inclinations, this would be a much different review. My Date With the President’s Daughter and What a Girl Wants and The Princess Diaries, all members of the canon to which this book belongs, were successful (to varying degrees) because the idea of the President or the Queen were distant, hazy fantasies rather than political and imperial figures. If Will Friedle had leveraged his relationship with President Richmond’s daughter to pass stricter gun legislation, the movie would have approximated the tone of this book. It’s a jarring, unwieldy juxtaposition.<br />Even if we leave all of the politics out of it, there isn’t much to redeem here. The sex scenes are jarring; in a break with modern romance conventions, CM describes the undressing and kissing in vivid, pages-long detail, then quickly skirts past sex. It reads like Harry Styles/Louis Tomlinson fanfiction written by someone who gets all of the angst but none of the mechanics. And this brings us to my theory: why this goddamn book?<br />Others have described this phenomenon in more depth--<a>these thoughts aren’t mine alone.</a> And I want to note before we get into it that I know CM isn’t straight. But when we look at who gets famous writing about young men falling in love with one another, we’re certainly not looking at a room full of men. By and large, the people who write this stuff are, as far as the publishing world and audiences at large perceive them, white women writing for a white woman audience. Regardless of their intentions and the complexities of their personal identities, that’s the lens through which their books are marketed and purchased. Publishers see the success of Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda and The Gentleman’s Guide to Vice and Virtue and they want more of the same--big on the pining and handsome young guys, light on the details of men having sex with each other. This book isn’t coming out because it’s a beautiful tale of gay love despite challenging circumstances. It’s coming out because some suits saw dollar signs.<br />So, let’s review: this book is painfully unaware of how painfully unaware it is; it’s an ice cream truck driving through an apocalyptic wasteland. Sure, ice cream rules, but are we just gonna ignore how utterly useless it is in the current landscape? And isn’t it a little offensive that it’s blaring “God Bless America”as it goes? Shouldn’t we feel a little miffed that someone thought to send us ice cream when we really need a damn life raft? There are many ways this book could have been a hell of a lot worse, but it’s not the story you deserve.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5444542250419328109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2713059454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2713059454" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2713059454?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2713059454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5213775373531948818">Alex Claremont-Diaz, First Son of the United States, is making his way through college, as well as plotting a future career in politics. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570401276ra/28254583.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>He already has years of experience working on various campaigns and is quite a successful schmoozer. Along with his sister and best friend, they navigate the D.C. social scene like it's their job; and it kind of is.<br/><br/>We all know I love political strategy in books, so right from the start, I'm digging the vibe.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559094429ra/27585802.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It quickly becomes obvious that Alex has some growing </span>
  <span id="freeText5213775373531948818" style="display:none">Alex Claremont-Diaz, First Son of the United States, is making his way through college, as well as plotting a future career in politics. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570401276ra/28254583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He already has years of experience working on various campaigns and is quite a successful schmoozer. Along with his sister and best friend, they navigate the D.C. social scene like it's their job; and it kind of is.<br><br>We all know I love political strategy in books, so right from the start, I'm digging the vibe.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559094429ra/27585802.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It quickly becomes obvious that Alex has some growing up to do. As he should, he's in his early-20s, y'all, give the boy a break! <br><br>He parties a little too hard, hooks up with randoms, who are then forced to sign NDAs and feuds with foreign dignitaries. <br><br>#relatable<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494548156ra/22727607.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alex's biggest rival is Prince Henry of the United Kingdom. <br><br>Henry is all sorts of swoony, exuding Prince Charming vibes, but Alex sees him as a total bore and his number one enemy. <br><br>When an embarrassing incident, involving both Alex and Henry, occurs at a royal wedding, the boys are forced to pretend to be friends in order to save face.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559094429ra/27585805.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alex would rather do pretty much anything else. <br><br>Unfortunately, his wants are inconsequential at this point, and so begins the relationship that will melt you; mind, body and soul.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466106764ra/19440854.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you are reading this, I am sure you already know what this book involves. It has received a lot of hype and for good reason. <br><br>A mainstream title, a humorous and steamy New Adult romance, featuring a male/male, enemies-to-lovers relationship? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496329411ra/22901871.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is basically <b>the book the world has been waiting for.</b> <br><br>And let's be honest, it's a book the world needs.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559094429ra/27585804.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I personally was swept away from the very first pages. It is so fun. Pure fun on the page, but also thoughtful in its presentation. <br><br>I truly feel this is ground-breaking and we will all be talking about it for years to come. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557073146ra/27461957.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>McQuiston did such a great job of making this so contemporary and natural. It never felt forced. <br><br>The dialogue was believable and the storyline provided a lot of food for thought.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559094429ra/27585803.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have heard a few people mention that it is too optimistic?<br><br>To me, I didn't really think so. It is a happy story overall, but our characters have struggles just like real people. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587727703ra/29348590.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alex and Henry both grapple with their sexuality and what that means in terms of their lives, their family's responses, the world's response; they really struggled with that. <br><br>There's no question, they had hard decisions to make, just like in real life.<br><br>As far as the overall outcome, I think we needed a book like this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Shouldn't we be striving for a world like this? <br><br>Where this could be a reality? Where the majority of the people would stand on the side of what is right instead of hiding behind the curtains of tradition? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I applaud Casey for writing this. I think this will mean a heck of a lot to a lot of people and McQuiston is definitely on my list of autobuy authors after this spectacular debut! Bravo!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587727703ra/29348591.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you so much to the publisher, St. Martin's Press, for providing me with a copy of this to read and review. <br><br>I always appreciate the opportunity. I think this will be making a lot of reader's 'Best of 2019' lists!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5213775373531948818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-and-a-half-stars">3-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2861320652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17300845974373042758">THIS IS THE CUTEST FLUFFIEST BOOK ON THE FACE OF THE PLANET.<br/><br/>This made me...blush? And I famously cannot blush. One time my high school English teacher overheard me saying I didn’t do the assigned reading and he called me out in front of the whole class, and I, like a tiny badass (pretending my heart wasn’t pounding and I wasn’t more nervous than I’ve ever been), was like “Yeah, I’m not trying to hide anything. I didn’t do the reading.” And he, taken aback, went, “...You’re not even blushing.”<br/><br/>So,</span>
  <span id="freeText17300845974373042758" style="display:none">THIS IS THE CUTEST FLUFFIEST BOOK ON THE FACE OF THE PLANET.<br /><br />This made me...blush? And I famously cannot blush. One time my high school English teacher overheard me saying I didn’t do the assigned reading and he called me out in front of the whole class, and I, like a tiny badass (pretending my heart wasn’t pounding and I wasn’t more nervous than I’ve ever been), was like “Yeah, I’m not trying to hide anything. I didn’t do the reading.” And he, taken aback, went, “...You’re not even blushing.”<br /><br />So, to recap: me, a school-obsessed profoundly shy 15-year-old being called out in front of all her very cool peers by her scary old man teacher = no blushing.<br /><br />The sheer adorableness of this book = Blush City, population me.<br /><br />CASEY MCQUISTON IS A STAR.<br /><br />This book has:<br />- amazing banter<br />- the best side characters <br />- fantastic friendships <br />- so much humor (I laughed! At a book! When does that HAPPEN!) <br />- tons of angst (actually too much angst sometimes - I got a little tired of this book towards the end) <br />- a great meet cute (except not actually a meeting. A re-meet-cute? Can I coin a term?)<br />- the best idea for a forbidden / enemies-to-lovers romance EVER!!! No exaggeration.<br /><br />So, in short, Casey McQuiston is, after just one book, a complete auto-buy author for me.<br /><br />However.<br /><br />This was not a perfect book. And in truth it made me cringe many times.<br /><br />Like, yes, on the one hand everyone is right and this is the cutest, fluffiest, most fun read of all time.<br /><br />On the other hand...I do not want my politics to be cute-fluffy-fun. I do not want them to be revisionist history where the current administration is absurdly well motivated and diverse and perfect and there is no corruption or back-hallway negotiation at all. It’s not realistic and to be honest, it makes me cringe.<br /><br />If I wanted an idealized-to-the-point-of-unbelievability fictional American president, I’d watch the West Wing and ignore the bigoted parts.<br /><br />I also think the scene with the Queen of England was Cringe Central. Again, not realistic, just completely good politics versus completely bad politics depending on which better serves the plot.<br /><br />This just felt...very juvenile. And I’m not saying that romance novels need to have the best ever take on politics. I’m not even saying that I was reading this book FOR the politics.<br /><br />All I’m saying is...I care about politics and seeing it idealized and completely unrealistic took me out of the story??<br /><br />(Can I say the word politics more.)<br /><br />Anyway. Even that was not enough to take away from this book so much for it to be a negative rating or an unenjoyable read.<br /><br />But...it was a takeaway. (SORRY.)<br /><br />Bottom line: Casey McQuiston give me your next book immediately please, and also thank you for not writing it about politics. (OKAY I’M DONE USING THE WORD POLITICS NOW.)<br /><br />----------<br /><br />nothing but respect for MY (alternate reality where the fictional president from this book is the actual) president<br /><br />review to come / 3.5 or 4 stars idk<br /><br />----------<br /><br />i'm a simple girl. i see a bajillion five star reviews of a contemporary, i read that contemporary</span>
  <a data-text-id="17300845974373042758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3104751328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14026259253162394581"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/><b>DNF @ 30% </b><br/><br/><br/><br/>Hey, did you know that this book is actually a love triangle? It's not just a love story between Alex and Henry. It's a love story between Alex and Henry and <i>everyone on Tumblr</i>.<b> </b>I have not read a book that wallows in its own sense of self-importance since, well, <i>ever</i>. This book won a Goodreads Choice Award. I had assumed it would be good because of that. But then again, SJM books also win GCAs and we know how I feel about <i>those</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14026259253162394581" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br><b>DNF @ 30% </b><br><br><br><br>Hey, did you know that this book is actually a love triangle? It's not just a love story between Alex and Henry. It's a love story between Alex and Henry and <i>everyone on Tumblr</i>.<b> </b>I have not read a book that wallows in its own sense of self-importance since, well, <i>ever</i>. This book won a Goodreads Choice Award. I had assumed it would be good because of that. But then again, SJM books also win GCAs and we know how I feel about <i>those</i>.<br><br><br><br><b></b><br>RED, WHITE &amp; ROYAL BLUE (where's the Oxford comma? I hate this book already) is a romance between the son of POTUS and the son of the royal family. If you would think that means serious political issues are going to be discussed-- HA! Think again. Instead it's falling into $75,000 wedding cakes and trading pop culture references about Harry Potter and Star Wars.<br><br><br><br><b></b><br>RW&amp;RB is a book that wants to let you know it's really, really hip. All of these references are going to mean nothing in ten years, but right now everyone is just nodding their heads and saying, "Yes, so topical!" When really, it's about as topical as a hemorrhoid cream. It reads like fanfic. I wouldn't be surprised if this started out as fanfic, but even if it didn't, it has that vibe. That vaguely fetishistic vibe that some books about gay men have that really bothers me, because it feels like they rely on stereotypes and head cannons and less about creating actual, realistic characters who are having an actual, realistic romance.<br><br><br><br><b></b><br>Henry and Alex are both SO IMMATURE. They have zero common sense, zero social savvy. Considering that they're both children of major heads of state, you would think that there would actually be some intelligence and grace somewhere in there, but no. Their "charm" consists of sarcastic grade school insults that we're supposed to believe is witty banter, and we're supposed to relate to them because they watch TV shows and read books that appeal to the 18-39 demographic, eat ice creams in the middle of the night, and use emojis! OMG THIS CHARACTER IS SO ME, A MILLENNIAL, AGE 18-39! I FEEL SEEN!<br><br><br><br><b></b><br>The female characters in this book, as others have pointed out, are all interchangeable. They are all basically stand-ins for the female audience, fawning over these two male characters, SHIPPING THEM SO HARD, and basically acting as the soulless Karen pod people they are, who all evolved from a single spore that bloomed out of a Harry/Draco fic on FF.net circa 2004.<br><br><br><br><b></b><br>I. Hated. This. Book.<br><br><br><br><b></b><br>I hate being pandered to, and I hate books that masquerade as intellectual and witty when they are, in fact, rather dull and unexceptional. If you want to read a <i>good </i>m-m romance that explores politics and fame while also being a provoking and incredibly romantic love story, read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3167007243" rel="nofollow noopener">THE GRAVITY OF US</a> (it's #ownvoices!). If you want to read vaguely fanficcy trash that at least doesn't pretend to be anything other than it is (i.e. vaguely fanficcy trash), read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1595393471" rel="nofollow noopener">THE CAPTIVE PRINCE</a> (warning: triggers abound). But if you want to read the "I'm vegan because I read the title of an article about free radicals in <i>People </i>magazine, and get all of my news from BuzzFeed articles and <i>The Young Turks</i>" version of an m-m love story, by all means, pick this up. #Bye<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>

<div id="review_2365125462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365125462" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365125462?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2019">best-of-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365125462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12781959645104849857"><b>This book is hilarious, thoughtful and devastatingly heartfelt.</b> Like I just really really enjoyed reading this?! I've been struggling to focus on books lately, but dude I stayed up very late reading this -- and also possibly sprained a rib from laughing so much. But perfect banter and adorable romance...what really took me was how heartfelt the book was, the characters were. It's a story about being brave enough to admit you are worth fighting for, for wanting things, and for chasing after those</span>
  <span id="freeText12781959645104849857" style="display:none"><b>This book is hilarious, thoughtful and devastatingly heartfelt.</b> Like I just really really enjoyed reading this?! I've been struggling to focus on books lately, but dude I stayed up very late reading this -- and also possibly sprained a rib from laughing so much. But perfect banter and adorable romance...what really took me was how heartfelt the book was, the characters were. It's a story about being brave enough to admit you are worth fighting for, for wanting things, and for chasing after those things. And <i>that</i>hit me in all sorts of emotional ways.<br /><br /><b>So basically the president's son and the prince of England have an unofficial rivalry...</b> which leads to a crush and a surprise-attack kiss and the very smack-in-the-face realisation that they've loved each other for a long long time. UGH IT WAS ADORABLE. It was also a lot of sex, lol, which reminded me why I stick to YA mostly. But I just loved how the romance was handled. There's angst yes, but their main issues was them vs the world...instead of angsty do-you-love-me-do-you-not which I am Not Fond Of. So thank you for that. Also I just ship these two idiots 😭Alex is 21 and doesn't even know he's bi and Henry is 23 and living so deeply undercover because the British Crown is not allowed to be gay, that he believes he doesn't even <i>deserve</i> to be happy. I just...these two. (Also their second kiss-scene? lmao.)<br /><br />also it was refreshing to read about Alex still figuring out his sexuality. His crisis was hilarious and endearing and relatable ajfkdslad and I just loved him. He's so brash and 10/10 to the moment where he stands in front of the palace swearing at Henry to come talk to him. Like THIS KID. Alex is an explosion, a mess, a heartfelt and emotional fire. Henry is stillness and smooth smiles and he's like a shot bullet, unchangeable, when he gets going. <br /><br /><b>And a moment for June and Nora.</b> Henry's sister and best friend respectively. Like they were the best, so clever, and the kind of women I love reading about. And give me the spin-off where they fall in love, u cowards, i need it.<br /><br /><b>The politics part?</b> I have no idea what's going on. No idea. All the politics scenes were pretty much lost on me, but I <i>did</i> like how driven and intelligent all the characters were. (It just made me feel like Gansey from The Raven Cycle would be at home with this lot ok.)<br /><br /><b>I can't even with how hilarious it was.</b> The banter was perfect and the quips were absolutely the best and I JUST. LOVED. THE. DIALOGUE.<br /><br />And look, it's definitely a sweet book with lots of fluffy scenes. Which I loved. (Although I could never relax, I always thought they'd get busted.) But it also touches on so many deeper topics: closeted queerness and actually how damaging that is to you, it explores what it is to be bi, it talks about oppression for women (specifically in politics) and for POC (Alex and June are biracial Mexican). And books always rob my heartbeat when they are about people who will fight for each other and their love. I turned into a sap in my old age, i shall not apologise.<br /><br /><br />*:·ﾟ✧*:·ﾟ✧ from the author's note:<br /><i>What I hoped to do, and what I hope I have done with this book by the time you've finished it, my dear reader: to be the spark of joy and hope you needed.</i><br /><br />Succeeded 1000%. I'm crying and my heart is so full. 😭</span>
  <a data-text-id="12781959645104849857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd"><img alt="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539540436p2/5138611.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" href="/user/show/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd">Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)</a>

<div id="review_2608215012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2608215012" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2608215012?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=soft-gay-babies">soft-gay-babies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=z-2019-reads">z-2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2608215012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1593313567869076987"><blockquote>
  <i>Alex, the First Son, has one arch-nemesis: Prince Henry of England, the Crown’s golden boy. After their long-held feud escalates to a disaster at the Royal Wedding, the two are forced to fake a friendship in the spotlight to smooth international relations, and it’s going to be absolutely terrible. After all, Alex hates Henry! … doesn’t he?</i>
</blockquote><br/>Okay, look, I don’t even know how to start this review so I’m just going to apologize in advance for my fangirling, because honestly, it’s really just NOT </span>
  <span id="freeText1593313567869076987" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Alex, the First Son, has one arch-nemesis: Prince Henry of England, the Crown’s golden boy. After their long-held feud escalates to a disaster at the Royal Wedding, the two are forced to fake a friendship in the spotlight to smooth international relations, and it’s going to be absolutely terrible. After all, Alex hates Henry! … doesn’t he?</i>
</blockquote><br />Okay, look, I don’t even know how to start this review so I’m just going to apologize in advance for my fangirling, because honestly, it’s really just NOT fair at all that we’re less than three months into the year and I’ve probably already found my favorite book of the year. I mean, <b>
  <i>HOLY HELL, Y’ALL, THIS IS SO GOOD.</i>
</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> “And you are good. Most things are awful most of the time, but you’re good.”</b>
</blockquote><br />I mean, this book is exactly what I’m referring to when I say that romance thrives on tropes and that we should embrace tropes more often because, seriously—international relations? Reluctant royals? Enemies-to-friends-to-lovers? Fake friendships? Fake dating? IT’S ALL HERE AND IT’S BEAUTIFUL. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> “The turkeys are not going to Jurassic Park you. You’re not the bloke from Seinfeld. You’re Jeff Goldblum.”</b>
</blockquote><br />When I say I loved this book, I’m worried that you’re interpreting it as, “wow, Destiny enjoyed this book,” when what I <b>mean</b> is, “I had to stop looking through my highlights for quotes to use because I was getting derailed by rereading all of my favorite parts and I’m legitimately tempted to reread this book right now even though I just finished it less than 24 hours ago.”<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> “You have so much in you, it’s almost impossible to match it. But he’s your match, dumbass.”</b>
</blockquote><br />There are so many freaking adorable characters that I want to cherish forever. I mean, SO MANY. And they’re all so flawlessly and casually diverse and precious and wonderful.<br />✨ <b>Alex:</b> First Son, biracial (white/Latinx), bisexual, hilarious, vaguely full of himself in the best way<br />👑 <b>Henry:</b> Prince, gaaaaay, softest bean ever<br />📰 <b>June:</b> First Daughter, biracial (white/Latinx), #squadmom for life, honestly gave me total queer vibes so can we please get a sequel confirming this??<br />💻 <b>Nora:</b> Alex and June’s bestie, bisexual, geeky AF, computer hacker and data analyst extraordinaire, endlessly hilarious (“still waters, deep dicking”)<br />🎤 <b>Bea:</b> Henry’s sister, former cocaine addict, sweet and feisty as hell, also queer AF and I’ll not hear any arguments<br />💎 <b>Pez:</b> Henry’s best friend, massive philanthropist, fashionista, no regard for societal gender roles (despite these last two things I’m tempted to think Pez is the Token Straight™ in the Super Six)<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>It’s nothing like kissing anyone he’s ever kissed in his life. It feels as steady and huge as the ground under their feet, as encompassing as every part of him, as likely to knock the wind out of his lungs.</b>
</blockquote><br />I could gush forever, honestly. And the humor in this story! I laughed out loud so many times. And the swooning! There’s a fair amount of sex (though the scenes are all tame and mostly vague if that’s something you’re worried about), and even when everyone is fully clothed, the tension is off the charts. They’re so sweet together and they wear their little hearts on their sleeves and I adored everything about the perfect OTP that is Alex and Henry. ♥ Also, their text and email conversations? KILL ME WITH CUTENESS, CASEY MCQUISTON, JUST DO IT.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>Whatever, fine. Henry is annoyingly attractive. That’s always been a thing, objectively. It’s fine.</b>
</blockquote><br />I think the last thing I want to say is just how optimistic and downright <b>hopeful</b> this book is. Without spoiling anything, there’s a scene towards the end that is just pure queer affirmation and support and love and it had me <b>bawling</b> the happiest tears at the thought. The world is a really ugly place sometimes (especially in US politics lately) and I cherished every moment of this escape and this view into what we’re hopefully moving towards.<br /><br /><i>All quotes come from an advance copy and may not match the final release. Thank you so much to St. Martin’s Press for providing me with this ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1593313567869076987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2827738448?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2827738448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2190918077086425805">its official. im now in a diabetic coma because my blood sugar levels are too high from how sweet this story is. its seriously too precious. its the perfect remedy for all your worries, troubles, and depression. and that is due to the boys - what sweet cinnamon rolls alex and henry are. to love this story is to love them. plain and simple. <br/><br/>i do think this would have been a 5 star read for me if it had been told in first person and from henrys POV. i think that would have made the writing much mo</span>
  <span id="freeText2190918077086425805" style="display:none">its official. im now in a diabetic coma because my blood sugar levels are too high from how sweet this story is. its seriously too precious. its the perfect remedy for all your worries, troubles, and depression. and that is due to the boys - what sweet cinnamon rolls alex and henry are. to love this story is to love them. plain and simple. <br /><br />i do think this would have been a 5 star read for me if it had been told in first person and from henrys POV. i think that would have made the writing much more relatable and not as forced, like it seemed to be at times. and it would have also saved me from all the dull american politics. i get enough of that IRL that i dont need it polluting such a nice and fluffy story. i would have much rather read about the royal family instead. i think those changes would have made this a much more perfect story for me personally. <br /><br />but all in all, i think this is deserving of all the hype its currently getting!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>
